## Frameworks

These frameworks make customizing your ZSH setup easier.

You can find some interesting performance timing comparisons of various frameworks in the following locations.

- <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;26â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;2ğŸ´</code></b> [rossmacarthur/zsh-plugin-manager-benchmark](https://github.com/rossmacarthur/zsh-plugin-manager-benchmark)
- <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;0â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;0ğŸ´</code></b> [pm-perf-test](https://github.com/z-shell/pm-perf-test) - Tooling for running performance tests on multiple ZSH frameworks.
### <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;91â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;19ğŸ´</code></b> [alf](https://github.com/psyrendust/alf)

**Alf** is an out of this world super fast and configurable framework for ZSH; it's modeled after Prezto and Antigen while utilizing Oh-My-Zsh under the covers; and offers standard defaults, aliases, functions, auto completion, automated updates and installable prompt themes and plugins.

### <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;254â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;74ğŸ´</code></b> [ansible-role-zsh](https://github.com/viasite-ansible/ansible-role-zsh)

**ansible-role-zsh** is an ansible role with zero-knowledge installation. It uses antigen to manage bundles and oh-my-zsh. Can load bundles conditionally. By default it includes powerlevel9k theme, autosuggestions, syntax-highlighting and <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;79â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;15ğŸ´</code></b> [fzf-widgets](https://github.com/ytet5uy4/fzf-widgets) and <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;389â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;33ğŸ´</code></b> [fzf-marks](https://github.com/urbainvaes/fzf-marks). Fully customizable.

### <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;26â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;3ğŸ´</code></b> [ant-zsh](https://github.com/anthraxx/ant-zsh)

**Ant-zsh** is a tiny and lightweight ZSH configuration environment for special customization needs. It includes plugins, themes and a basic convenient setup.

### <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;1682â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;61ğŸ´</code></b> [antibody](https://github.com/getantibody/antibody)

**Antibody** is a faster and simpler antigen written in Golang. More details at ğŸŒ [http://getantibody.github.io/](http://getantibody.github.io/).

### <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;27â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;1ğŸ´</code></b> [antidote](https://github.com/mattmc3/antidote)

**Antidote** is a faster, simpler antigen, written in native Zsh. It picks up where antibody left off.

### <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;202â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;21ğŸ´</code></b> [antigen-hs](https://github.com/Tarrasch/antigen-hs)

**antigen-hs** is a replacement for antigen optimized for a low overhead when starting up the shell. It will automatically clone plugins for you.

### <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;6952â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;273ğŸ´</code></b> [antigen](https://github.com/zsh-users/antigen)

**Antigen** is a small set of functions that help you easily manage your shell (ZSH) plugins, called bundles. The concept is pretty much the same as bundles in a typical vim+pathogen setup. Antigen is to ZSH, what Vundle is to vim. Antigen can load oh-my-zsh themes and plugins and will automatically clone them for you.

### <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;11â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;1ğŸ´</code></b> [ax-zsh](https://github.com/alexbarton/ax-zsh)

**Ax-ZSH** is a modular configuration system for ZSH. It provides sane defaults and is extendable by plugins.

**Ax-ZSH** integrates well with <b><code>&nbsp;26024â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;1382ğŸ´</code></b> [Powerlevel10k](https://github.com/romkatv/powerlevel10k) and other extensions, including plugins compatible with ğŸŒ [oh-my-zsh](https://ohmyz.sh/).

### <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;201â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;36ğŸ´</code></b> [dotzsh](https://github.com/dotphiles/dotzsh)

**Dotzsh** strives to be platform and version independent. Some functionality may be lost when running under older versions of ZSH, but it should degrade cleanly and allow you to use the same setup on multiple machines of differing OSes without problems.

### <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;1076â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;92ğŸ´</code></b> [fresh](https://github.com/freshshell/fresh)

**fresh** is a tool to source shell configuration (aliases, functions, etc) from others into your own configuration files. We also support files such as ackrc and gitconfig. Think of it as Bundler for your dot files.

### ğŸŒ [miniplug](https://sr.ht/~yerinalexey/miniplug)

**miniplug** is a minimalistic plugin manager for ZSH.

- No crashes or double plugin loading when re-sourcing .zshrc
- Unlike other frameworks, Miniplug does not pollute your $PATH
- Only does the bare minimum for managing plugins

### <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;3â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;1ğŸ´</code></b> [mzpm](https://github.com/Insert-Creative-Name-Here/mzpm)

**mzpm** is a minimalist plugin manager for ZSH.

Features:

- Fetching and loading plugins from GitHub
- Loading local plugins
- Loading themes

### ğŸŒ [oh-my-zsh](https://ohmyz.sh/)

**oh-my-zsh** is a community-driven framework for managing your ZSH configuration. Includes 120+ optional plugins (rails, git, macOS, hub, capistrano, brew, ant, macports, etc), over 120 themes to spice up your morning, and an auto-update tool that makes it easy to keep up with the latest updates from the community.

### <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;3â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;0ğŸ´</code></b> [PMS](https://github.com/JoshuaEstes/pms)

PMS allows you to manage your shell in a way to that helps decrease setup time and increases your productivity. It has support for themes (change the way your shell looks), plugins (adds functionality to your shell), and dotfile management.

The PMS framework also allows you to use the same framework in different shells. Use ZSH on your personal laptop, and use bash on remote servers. Wanna try fish? Go ahead, try out different shells.

### <b><code>&nbsp;12635â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;4440ğŸ´</code></b> [prezto](https://github.com/sorin-ionescu/prezto)

**Prezto** enriches the ZSH command line interface environment with sane defaults, aliases, functions, auto completion, and prompt themes. There are some prezto-specific plugins at <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;100â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;41ğŸ´</code></b> [https://github.com/belak/prezto-contrib](https://github.com/belak/prezto-contrib).

### <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;8â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;1ğŸ´</code></b> [pumice](https://github.com/ryutamaki/pumice)

**Pumice** is a lightweight plugin manager for ZSH.

### <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;320â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;11ğŸ´</code></b> [sheldon](https://github.com/rossmacarthur/sheldon)

A fast, configurable, shell plugin manager.

- Can manage
  - Any `git` repository.
    - Branch/tag/commit support.
    - Extra support for GitHub repositories.
    - Extra support for Gists.
  - Arbitrary remote files, simply specify the URL.
  - Local plugins, simply specify the directory path.
- Highly configurable install methods using ğŸŒ [handlebars](http://handlebarsjs.com/) templating.
- Super-fast parallel installation.
- Configuration file using <b><code>&nbsp;16694â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;805ğŸ´</code></b> [TOML](https://github.com/toml-lang/toml) syntax.
- Uses a lock file for much faster loading of plugins.

### <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;11â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;1ğŸ´</code></b> [Toasty](https://github.com/5paceToast/toasty-zsh)

**Toasty** is a ZSH framework made to facilitate management, not dictate it.

### <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;1â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;0ğŸ´</code></b> [tzpm](https://github.com/notusknot/tzpm)

The tiniest ZSH plugin manager. Still under development.

### <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;5â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;4ğŸ´</code></b> [uz](https://github.com/maxrodrigo/uz)

A ZSH micro plugin manager.

### <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;0â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;0ğŸ´</code></b> [yazt](https://github.com/bashelled/yazt)

Yazt is a simple zsh theme manager in maintence that is compatible with nearly everything. You can use prompts in plugins, mix 'n' match two themes, with a few modifications, you can even use it in bash.

### <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;7â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;1ğŸ´</code></b> [zapack](https://github.com/aiya000/zsh-zapack)

zapack is a basic fast minimal ZSH plugin loader.

### <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;102â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;6ğŸ´</code></b> [zcomet](https://github.com/agkozak/zcomet)

**zcomet** is a minimalistic ZSH plugin manager that gets you to the prompt surprisingly quickly without caching (see the benchmarks). In addition to loading and updating plugins stored in Git repositories, it supports lazy-loading plugins (further reducing startup time) as well as downloading and sourcing code snippets.

### <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;40â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;8ğŸ´</code></b> [zeesh](https://github.com/zeekay/zeesh)

**Zeesh** is a cross-platform ZSH framework. It's similar to, but incompatible with, ğŸŒ [oh-my-zsh](http://ohmyz.sh/). It has a modular plugin architecture making it easy to extend. It has a rich set of defaults, but is designed to be as lightweight as possible.

### <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;10â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;1ğŸ´</code></b> [zgem](https://github.com/qoomon/zgem)

**Zgem** is a plugin manager for ZSH that supports loading and updating plugins and themes from git, http and local files.

### <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;1360â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;103ğŸ´</code></b> [zgen](https://github.com/tarjoilija/zgen)

**Zgen** is a lightweight plugin manager for ZSH inspired by Antigen. The goal is to have minimal overhead when starting up the shell because nobody likes waiting. It is currently not being actively maintained and I recommend you use the <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;168â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;8ğŸ´</code></b> [zgenom](https://github.com/jandamm/zgenom) fork instead, which is.

### <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;168â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;8ğŸ´</code></b> [zgenom](https://github.com/jandamm/zgenom)

A lightweight plugin manager for ZSH that is a fork that extends the brilliant <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;1360â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;103ğŸ´</code></b> [zgen](https://github.com/tarjoilija/zgen) and provides more features and bugfixes while being fully backwards compatible.

To keep loading fast during new terminal sessions, `zgenom` generates a static `init.zsh` file which does nothing but source your plugins and append them to your `fpath`.

This minimizes startup time by not having to execute time consuming logic (plugin checking, updates, etc) during startup. The downside is that you have to refresh the init script manually with `zgenom reset` whenever you update your plugin list in your `.zshrc`.

Zgenom can load ğŸŒ [oh-my-zsh](http://ohmyz.sh/)-compatible and <b><code>&nbsp;12635â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;4440ğŸ´</code></b> [prezto](https://github.com/sorin-ionescu/prezto)-compatible plugins and themes, and will automagically `git clone` plugins for you when you add them to your plugin list.

### <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;95â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;9ğŸ´</code></b> [ZI](https://github.com/z-shell/zi)

**ZI** is a Swiss Army Knife for Zsh Unix shell. Formerly known as zplugin, zinit. ZI - ğŸŒ [Wiki Pages](https://z-shell.pages.dev/).

Bonus: you can use <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;1â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;2ğŸ´</code></b> [zi-console](https://github.com/z-shell/zi-console) to view and change the state of the ZSH session (e.g.: list and unload plugins) and to delete the plugins and snippets from the disk.

### <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;32â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;3ğŸ´</code></b> [zilsh](https://github.com/zilsh/zilsh)

**zilsh** is a ZSH config system that aims to appeal more to power-users and follow the simplistic approach of vim-pathogen.

### <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;2341â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;164ğŸ´</code></b> [zim](https://github.com/zimfw/zimfw)

**Zim** is a ZSH configuration framework with blazing speed and modular extensions.

### <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;796â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;87ğŸ´</code></b> [Zinit](https://github.com/zdharma-continuum/zinit)

**Zinit** is an innovative and probably (because of the Turbo) the fastest plugin manager with support for:

- Turbo mode â€“ 80% faster ZSH startup! for example: instead of 200 ms, it'll be 40 ms
- Completion management (selectively disable and enable completions)
- Snippets (â†” regular files downloaded via-URL, e.g.: scripts) and through them Oh My Zsh and Prezto plugins support (â†’ low overhead)
- Annexes (â†” Zinit extensions)
- Reports (from the plugin loads â€“ plugins are no longer black boxes)
- Plugin unloading (allows e.g.: dynamic theme switching)
- `bindkey` capturing and remapping
- packages
- Clean `fpath` (the array `$fpath` is not being used to add completions and autoload functions, hence it stays concise, not bloated)
- Services â†” a single-instance, background plugins
- Also, in general: all the mechanisms from the ZSH Plugin Standard â€“ Zinit is a reference implementation of the standard.

The project is very active â€“ currently > 3100 commits.

### <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;25â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;3ğŸ´</code></b> [zit](https://github.com/thiagokokada/zit)

**zit** is a plugin manager for ZSH. It is minimal because it implements the bare minimum to be qualified as a plugin manager: it allows the user to install plugins from Git repositories (and Git repositories only, them why the name), source plugins and update them. It does not implement fancy functions like cleanup of removed plugins, automatic compilation of installed plugins, alias for oh-my-zsh/prezto/other ZSH frameworks, building binaries, PATH manipulation and others.

### <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;412â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;15ğŸ´</code></b> [znap](https://github.com/marlonrichert/zsh-snap)

**:zap:Znap** is a light-weight plugin manager & Git repo manager for ZSH that's easy to grok. While tailored for ZSH plugins specifically, Znap also functions as a general-pupose utility for managing Git repos.

Znap

Znap can:

- Make any prompt appear instantly. Reduce your startup time from ~200ms to ~40ms with just one command.
- Asynchronously compile your plugins and functions.
- Cache those expensive `eval $(commands)`.
- Clone or pull multiple repos in parallel.
- Re-clone all your repos without you having to re-enter them.
- Multi-repo management
- Automatic `compinit` and `bashinit` - you no longer need them in your `.zshrc`, znap will do them automatically as needed.

### <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;31â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;4ğŸ´</code></b> [zoppo](https://github.com/zoppo/zoppo)

**Zoppo** is the crippled configuration framework for ZSH. As an Italian saying goes: "chi va con lo zoppo, impara a zoppicare", we realized we were walking with a cripple and are now going to become crippled ourselves.

### <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;2â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;0ğŸ´</code></b> [zpacker](https://github.com/happyslowly/zpacker)

**Zpacker** is a lightweight ZSH plugin & theme management framework.

### <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;1â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;0ğŸ´</code></b> [zpico](https://github.com/thornjad/zpico)

The minuscule ZSH package manager. No frills, no bloat, just 2 kB of 100% ZSH code, providing complete package management for your ZSH environment.

### <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;4938â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;215ğŸ´</code></b> [zplug](https://github.com/zplug/zplug)

**:hibiscus: Zplug** is a next-generation ZSH plugin manager.

- Can manage everything
  - Zsh plugins/UNIX commands on ğŸŒ [GitHub](https://github.com) and ğŸŒ [Bitbucket](https://bitbucket.org)
  - Gist files  ğŸŒ [gist.github.com](https://gist.github.com/discover))
  - Externally managed plugins e.g., <b><code>141726â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;23745ğŸ´</code></b> [oh-my-zsh](https://github.com/ohmyzsh/ohmyzsh) and <b><code>&nbsp;12635â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;4440ğŸ´</code></b> [prezto](https://github.com/sorin-ionescu/prezto) plugins/themes
  - Binary artifacts on ğŸŒ [GitHub Releases](https://help.github.com/articles/about-releases/)
  - Local plugins
  - etc. (you can add your <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;?â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;?ğŸ´</code></b> [own sources](https://github.com/zplug/zplug/blob/master/doc/guide/External-Sources.md)!)
- Super-fast parallel installation/update
- Support for lazy-loading
- Branch/tag/commit support
- Post-update, post-load hooks
- Dependencies between packages
- Unlike <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;6952â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;273ğŸ´</code></b> [antigen](https://github.com/zsh-users/antigen), no ZSH plugin file (`*.plugin.zsh`) required
- Interactive interface  <b><code>&nbsp;42468â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;1856ğŸ´</code></b> [fzf](https://github.com/junegunn/fzf), <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;6790â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;225ğŸ´</code></b> [peco](https://github.com/peco/peco), <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;516â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;70ğŸ´</code></b> [zaw](https://github.com/zsh-users/zaw), and so on)
- Cache mechanism for reducing <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;4938â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;215ğŸ´</code></b> [the startup time](https://github.com/zplug/zplug#vs)

### <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;218â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;11ğŸ´</code></b> [zpm](https://github.com/zpm-zsh/zpm)

**zpm** ( ZSH Plugin Manager ) is a plugin manager for ğŸŒ [ZSH](http://www.zsh.org/) who combines the imperative and declarative approach. At first run, zpm will do complex logic and generate cache, after that will be used cache only, so it makes this framework to be very fast.

- Fastest plugin manager (Really, after the first run, zpm will not be used at all)
- Support for async loading
- Dependencies between packages
- zpm runs on Linux, macOS, FreeBSD and Android.
- zpm plugins are compatible with ğŸŒ [oh-my-zsh](http://ohmyz.sh/).

### <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;130â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;8ğŸ´</code></b> [zr](https://github.com/jedahan/zr)

**zr** is a quick, simple ZSH plugin manager written in Rust and easily installable with `cargo install zr`.

### <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;7â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;2ğŸ´</code></b> [zshing](https://github.com/zakariaGatter/zshing)

**zshing** is a ZSH plugin manager similar to Vundle/Vim and allows you to...

- keep track of and configure your plugins right in the `.zshrc`
- Install ZSH plugins
- Update ZSH plugins
- Search by name all available ZSH Plugins
- Clean unused plugins up
- run the above actions in a *single command*
- manages the __Source Plugins__ of your installed Plugins

### <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;264â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;55ğŸ´</code></b> [ztanesh](https://github.com/miohtama/ztanesh)

**Ztanesh** aims to improve your UNIX command line experience and productivity with the the configuration provided by the ztanesh project: the tools will make your shell more powerful and easier to use.

### <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;2â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;1ğŸ´</code></b> [ztheme](https://github.com/SkyyySi/ztheme)

ztheme is a small and fast theme engine for ZSH.

### <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;4â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;0ğŸ´</code></b> [ztupide](https://github.com/mpostaire/ztupide)

A simple and fast ZSH plugin manager. It uses zcompile and async loading to speed up your shell startup time.

### <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;136â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;14ğŸ´</code></b> [zulu](https://github.com/zulu-zsh/zulu)

**Zulu** is a environment manager for ZSH 5+, which aims to make it easy to manage your shell without writing any code.

- Easily manage your shell environment without editing files.
- Create aliases, functions and environment variables, and have them available to you at the next shell startup.
- Add and remove directories from `$path`, `$fpath` and `$cdpath` with simple commands.
- Install packages, plugins and themes easily, and have them available to you immediately.

## Setups

This section is for full setup dropins - they aren't frameworks, but they're not simple plugins/themes either.

### zgenom

- <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;509â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;77ğŸ´</code></b> [zsh-quickstart-kit](https://github.com/unixorn/zsh-quickstart-kit) - A simple quickstart for using ZSH with <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;168â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;8ğŸ´</code></b> [zgenom](https://github.com/jandamm/zgenom). This automatically configures ZSH to use <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;168â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;8ğŸ´</code></b> [zgenom](https://github.com/jandamm/zgenom) to load a curated collection of plugins and periodically automatically update itself, the plugins, and the quickstart kit itself.

### zinit

- <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;86â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;6ğŸ´</code></b> [ZPWR](https://github.com/MenkeTechnologies/zpwr) - An extremely powerful custom terminal environment built on top of <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;796â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;87ğŸ´</code></b> [Zinit](https://github.com/zdharma-continuum/zinit) for maximum speed.  A full terminal configuration framework including `zsh`, `tmux`, `fzf`, `vim` and spacemacs configurations.  It includes:

- 11.5k+ tab completions
- 1.9k+ aliases
- 330+ git aliases
- 350+ zpwr subcommands
- 2.1k functions
- 150+ zpwr environment variables
- 170+ perl, python, bash, zsh scripts
- 2.8k line README.md
- 46k+ LOC
- 1 line install

- ğŸŒ [A Beautifully Productive Terminal Experience](https://mikebuss.com/2014/02/02/a-beautiful-productive-terminal-experience/) - Tutorial using a combination of ğŸŒ [iTerm 2](https://www.iterm2.com/#/section/home), ğŸŒ [ZSH](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Z_shell), <b><code>&nbsp;12635â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;4440ğŸ´</code></b> [Prezto](https://github.com/sorin-ionescu/prezto), ğŸŒ [Tmux](https://tmux.github.io), and <b><code>&nbsp;11203â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;613ğŸ´</code></b> [Tmuxinator](https://github.com/tmuxinator/tmuxinator) to make for an extremely productive developer workflow.

Installs <b><code>&nbsp;26024â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;1382ğŸ´</code></b> [Powerlevel10k](https://github.com/romkatv/powerlevel10k), <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;5090â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;619ğŸ´</code></b> [zsh-completions](https://github.com/zsh-users/zsh-completions), <b><code>&nbsp;20797â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;1324ğŸ´</code></b> [zsh-autosuggestions](https://github.com/zsh-users/zsh-autosuggestions), <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;?â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;?ğŸ´</code></b> [fast-syntax-highlighting](https://github.com/zdharma-continuum/fast-syntax-highlighting/), and more.

### ZSH on Windows

#### <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;48â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;2ğŸ´</code></b> [superconsole](https://github.com/alexchmykhalo/superconsole) - Windows-only.

  - `ConEmu`/`zsh` out-of-the-box configured to restore previously opened tabs and shell working directories after `ConEmu` restart
  - Choose between clean and inherited environment when starting new SuperConsole sessions
  - Custom colorful scheme, colorful output for various commands
  - `MSYS2` included, `zsh` and necessary software preinstalled, uses zsh-grml-config
  - Uses <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;6952â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;273ğŸ´</code></b> [Antigen](https://github.com/zsh-users/antigen) for ZSH theme and config management
  - Enabled number of ZSH plugins to activate completion, highlighting and history for most comfortable use
  - Git-for-Windows repo with proper `git` and `git lfs` support for `MSYS2` environment is configured, `git` client already installed.
  - `ssh-agent` for `git` works out-of-box, add your keys to `ConEmu/msys64/ConEmu/msys64/home/user/.ssh` dir
  - Non-blocking ZSH prompt status updates thanks to <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;220â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;27ğŸ´</code></b> [agkozak-zsh-prompt](https://github.com/agkozak/agkozak-zsh-prompt)
  - Command-not-found handler customized for `MSYS2` suggests what package to install
  - Sets up `nano` as main editor, enables `nano` syntax highlighting
  - Custom helper scripts added to `ConEmu/msys64/3rdparty`

## Plugins

- <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;3â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;0ğŸ´</code></b> [1999](https://github.com/DTan13/zsh1999) - Powerline-esque theme. Includes `git` status decorations, network and battery status.
- <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;117â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;10ğŸ´</code></b> [256color](https://github.com/chrissicool/zsh-256color) - Enhances the terminal environment with 256 colors. It looks at the chosen `TERM` environment variable and sees if there is respective ncurses' terminfo with 256 colors available. The result is a multicolor terminal, if available.
- <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;226â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;11ğŸ´</code></b> [abbr (olets)](https://github.com/olets/zsh-abbr) - Manages auto-expanding abbreviations that expand inline when you hit space, inspired by fish shell.
- <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;7â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;4ğŸ´</code></b> [abbr-path](https://github.com/felixgravila/zsh-abbr-path) - Adds functionality of the `theme_title_use_abbreviated_path` parameter from some oh-my-fish themes.
- <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;96â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;9ğŸ´</code></b> [abbrev-alias](https://github.com/momo-lab/zsh-abbrev-alias) - Provides functionality similar to `vim`'s abbreviation expansion.
- <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;1â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;0ğŸ´</code></b> [accurev](https://github.com/dalefukami/accurev-zsh) - ZSH plugin for ğŸŒ [accurev](https://www.microfocus.com/en-us/products/accurev/overview).
- <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;1â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;2ğŸ´</code></b> [actiona](https://github.com/matthieusb/act) - Make it easier to call <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;301â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;45ğŸ´</code></b> [actiona](https://github.com/Jmgr/actiona) scripts from your command line. Includes tab completions.
- <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;0â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;0ğŸ´</code></b> [activate-py-environment](https://github.com/se-jaeger/zsh-activate-py-environment) - Automagically detects and activates your python environments (poetry, virtualenv, conda) while traversing directories.
- <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;3â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;0ğŸ´</code></b> [alacritty](https://github.com/casonadams/alacritty-shell) - Control <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;?â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;?ğŸ´</code></b> [alacritty](https://github.com/alacritty/alacritty/wiki/Color-schemes) color schemes.
- <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;7â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;2ğŸ´</code></b> [alehouse](https://github.com/sticklerm3/alehouse) - Contains short aliases for ğŸŒ [brew](https://brew.sh) commands, inspired by <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;11â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;0ğŸ´</code></b> [betterbrew](https://github.com/timothyrowan/betterbrew-zsh-plugin).
- <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;605â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;43ğŸ´</code></b> [alias-tips](https://github.com/djui/alias-tips) - An oh-my-zsh plugin to help remembering those aliases you defined once.
- <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;0â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;0ğŸ´</code></b> [alias](https://github.com/xylous/alias-zsh) - Tool for managing your aliases.
- <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;2â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;1ğŸ´</code></b> [allergen](https://github.com/stanislas/allergen) - A collection of custom ZSH plugins to use with Antigen.
- <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;81â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;6ğŸ´</code></b> [almostontop](https://github.com/Valiev/almostontop) - Clears previous command output every time before new command executed in shell. Inspired by the <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;184â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;24ğŸ´</code></b> [alwaysontop](https://github.com/swirepe/alwaysontop) plugin for `bash`.
- <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;1â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;0ğŸ´</code></b> [alt-and-select](https://github.com/raisty/alt-and-select) - Binds the alt-c (copy), alt-v (paste), alt-x (cut) keyboard shortcut to a commands: copy-region-as-kill, yank, kill-region. Remaps the execute command to Alt-Shift-X.
- <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;10â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;1ğŸ´</code></b> [ansible](https://github.com/sparsick/ansible-zsh) - A plugin for ğŸŒ [Ansible](https://www.ansible.com/).

- <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;6â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;1ğŸ´</code></b> [apache2](https://github.com/voronkovich/apache2.plugin.zsh) - Adds aliases and functions for managing Apache2.
- <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;12â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;1ğŸ´</code></b> [apparix](https://github.com/micans/apparix) - Command line directory bookmarks with jumping to bookmarks, subdirectory tab completion, distant listing etc.
- <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;301â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;14ğŸ´</code></b> [apple-touchbar](https://github.com/zsh-users/zsh-apple-touchbar) - Adds MacBook Pro touchbar support in ğŸŒ [iTerm 2](https://iterm2.com).
- <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;12â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;2ğŸ´</code></b> [appup](https://github.com/Cloudstek/zsh-plugin-appup) - Adds `start`, `stop`, `up` and `down` commands when it detects a `docker-compose.yml` or `Vagrantfile` in the current directory (e.g. your application). Just run `up` and get coding!
- <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;5â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;0ğŸ´</code></b> [arc](https://github.com/anton-rudeshko/zsh-arc) - Adds aliases for Yandex version control system.
- <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;2â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;0ğŸ´</code></b> [arduino](https://github.com/raghur/zsh-arduino) - Adds scripts to build, upload and monitor arduino sketches from a command line. Requires ğŸŒ [`jq`](https://stedolan.github.io/jq/).
- <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;401â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;17ğŸ´</code></b> [artisan](https://github.com/jessarcher/zsh-artisan) - Laravel `artisan` plugin for ZSH to help you to run `artisan` from anywhere in the project tree, with tab completion!
- <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;4â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;0ğŸ´</code></b> [asciidoctor](https://github.com/sparsick/asciidoctor-zsh) - A plugin for AsciiDoctor.
- <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;3â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;0ğŸ´</code></b> [asdf-direnv](https://github.com/redxtech/zsh-asdf-direnv) - Integration and completions for <b><code>&nbsp;13396â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;541ğŸ´</code></b> [asdf](https://github.com/asdf-vm/asdf) and <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;273â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;18ğŸ´</code></b> [direnv](https://github.com/asdf-community/asdf-direnv).
- <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;1â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;0ğŸ´</code></b> [asdf-prompt](https://github.com/CurryEleison/zsh-asdf-prompt) - Provides a function usable in prompts that displays version information for your current tool versions.
- <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;11â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;6ğŸ´</code></b> [asdf](https://github.com/kiurchv/asdf.plugin.zsh) - Integration and completions for <b><code>&nbsp;13396â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;541ğŸ´</code></b> [asdf](https://github.com/asdf-vm/asdf), the extendable version manager, with support for Ruby, Node.js, Elixir, Erlang and more.
- <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;4â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;1ğŸ´</code></b> [assume-role](https://github.com/weizard/assume-role) - ZSH plugin to allow you to assume AWS IAM roles easily. Includes completions.
- <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;604â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;27ğŸ´</code></b> [async](https://github.com/mafredri/zsh-async) - Library for running asynchronous tasks in ZSH without requiring any external tools. Allows you to run multiple asynchronous jobs, enforce unique jobs (multiple instances of the same job will not run), flush all currently running jobs and create multiple workers (each with their own jobs).
- <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;4â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;2ğŸ´</code></b> [atom-plugin](https://github.com/CorradoRossi/oh-my-zsh-atom-plugin) - Based on the <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;3â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;0ğŸ´</code></b> [Sublime](https://github.com/valentinocossar/sublime) plugin, lets you launch a file or folder in ğŸŒ [Atom](https://atom.io) from ğŸŒ [iTerm 2](https://iterm2.com).
- <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;1444â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;57ğŸ´</code></b> [atuin](https://github.com/ellie/atuin) - Replaces your existing shell history with a SQLite database, and records additional context for your commands. Additionally, it provides optional and fully encrypted synchronisation of your history between machines, via an Atuin server.

- <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;4â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;0ğŸ´</code></b> [zinsults](https://github.com/ahmubashshir/zinsults) - Prints insults if a command fails.

## Completions

These plugins add tab completions without adding extra functions or aliases.

- <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;3â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;0ğŸ´</code></b> [_url-httplink](https://github.com/Valodim/zsh-_url-httplink) - Extends ZSH's \_urls completion, allowing it to complete urls from html pages.
- <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;0â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;0ğŸ´</code></b> [aliyun](https://github.com/thuandt/zsh-aliyun) - Add completions for the <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;622â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;180ğŸ´</code></b> [Aliyun CLI](https://github.com/aliyun/aliyun-cli).
- <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;2â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;1ğŸ´</code></b> [ansible-server](https://github.com/viasite-ansible/zsh-ansible-server) - Completions for viasite-ansible/ansible-server.
- <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;0â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;0ğŸ´</code></b> [antibody-completion](https://github.com/sinetoami/antibody-completion) - This plugin provides completion for <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;1682â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;61ğŸ´</code></b> [Antibody](https://github.com/getantibody/antibody) plugin manager.

- <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;9â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;2ğŸ´</code></b> [autopkg-zsh-completion](https://github.com/fuzzylogiq/autopkg-zsh-completion) - Completions for autopkg.

- <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;532â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;15ğŸ´</code></b> [yarn](https://github.com/g-plane/zsh-yarn-autocompletions) - Add autocompletions for `yarn add`, `yarn remove`, `yarn upgrade`, `yarn why` and `yarn run`.
- <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;8â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;3ğŸ´</code></b> [zargparse](https://github.com/ctil/zargparse) - Pass it a script that uses `argparse` and it will write a ZSH completion to your current directory.
- <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;?â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;?ğŸ´</code></b> [zstyle-completions](https://github.com/zshzoo/zstyle-completions) - Gives <b><code>&nbsp;12635â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;4440ğŸ´</code></b> [prezto-style](https://github.com/sorin-ionescu/prezto) completions when you hit tab.

## Themes

If you're using <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;6952â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;273ğŸ´</code></b> [Antigen](https://github.com/zsh-users/antigen), you can test these themes in a running ZSH with `antigen theme githubuser/repo`. If you're using <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;168â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;8ğŸ´</code></b> [zgenom](https://github.com/jandamm/zgenom), add them to your `init.zsh` with `zgenom load githubuser/reponame`.

- <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;0â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;0ğŸ´</code></b> [000](https://github.com/Abid-Ahmad/oh-my-zsh-000-theme) - Multiline prompt with username, hostname, full path, return status and `git` decorations.
- <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;10â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;2ğŸ´</code></b> [0i0](https://github.com/0i0/0i0.zsh-theme) - Optimized for dark terminal windows, uses nerdfont `git` status decorations.
- <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;?â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;?ğŸ´</code></b> [14degree](https://github.com/saims0n/14degree-zsh-theme/) - Includes `git`, `virtualenv` and `rvm` status decorations.
- <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;0â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;0ğŸ´</code></b> [4den](https://github.com/RunThem/zsh-theme-4den) - Minimalist. Includes `git` and `hg` status decorations.
- <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;3â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;3ğŸ´</code></b> [aaron](https://github.com/aaronjamesyoung/aaron-zsh-theme) - Based on the Sorin theme.
- <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;1â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;1ğŸ´</code></b> [abbr (theme)](https://github.com/PhilsLab/abbr-zsh-theme) - Displays an abbreviated version of the current directory path, shows the Python virtualenv, Rust version, `git` status, and the exit code of last command. Works well on dark backgrounds by default but colors can be easily customized.
- <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;33â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;4ğŸ´</code></b> [absolute](https://github.com/NelsonBrandao/absolute) - Very clean looking theme with git status, node version and the exit code from the last command.
- <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;1â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;2ğŸ´</code></b> [adamdodev](https://github.com/adamdodev/adamdodev-zsh-theme) - Includes `git` status decorations, name of your AWS profile, name of your Azure Service Principal, kubernetes context, terraform workspace, command status and current working directory.
- <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;?â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;?ğŸ´</code></b> [adlee](https://github.com/adlee-was-taken/oh-my-zsh-osx/blob/master/adlee.zsh-theme) - macOS theme, requires a Powerline-compatible font.
- <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;1â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;0ğŸ´</code></b> [af-magic-dynamic](https://github.com/rslavin/af-magic-dynamic) - Modified version of <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;?â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;?ğŸ´</code></b> [af-magic](https://github.com/andyfleming/oh-my-zsh/blob/master/themes/af-magic.zsh-theme) with dynamic path shortening.
- ğŸŒ [af-magic-mod](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/desyncr/zshrc/master/themes/af-magic-mod.zsh-theme) - af-magic-mod theme.
- <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;0â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;0ğŸ´</code></b> [aflah-bhari](https://github.com/AflahB/aflah-bhari-zsh-theme) - Modified version of the <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;?â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;?ğŸ´</code></b> [robbyrussell](https://github.com/ohmyzsh/ohmyzsh/blob/master/themes/robbyrussell.zsh-theme) theme in oh-my-zsh.
- <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;2â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;0ğŸ´</code></b> [aftermath](https://github.com/schanur/aftermath) - Get a nice summary line after each command you run in your shell.
- <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;5â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;3ğŸ´</code></b> [agitnoster](https://github.com/dbestevez/agitnoster-theme) - Based on ğŸŒ [agnoster](https://gist.github.com/3712874) theme included in <b><code>141726â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;23745ğŸ´</code></b> [Oh My Zsh](https://github.com/ohmyzsh/ohmyzsh) and <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;6197â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;918ğŸ´</code></b> [bash-git-prompt](https://github.com/magicmonty/bash-git-prompt). Shows detailed information about `git` status.
- <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;220â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;27ğŸ´</code></b> [agkozak](https://github.com/agkozak/agkozak-zsh-prompt) - Uses three asynchronous methods to keep the ZSH prompt responsive while displaying the `git` status and indicators of SSH connection, exit codes, and `vi` mode, along with an abbreviated, `PROMPT_DIRTRIM`-style path. Very customizable. Asynchronous even on Cygwin and MSYS2.
- <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;240â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;58ğŸ´</code></b> [agnoster-fcamblor](https://github.com/fcamblor/oh-my-zsh-agnoster-fcamblor) - Solarized ğŸŒ [Agnoster](https://gist.github.com/agnoster/3712874) variant with `git` status information. Requires a unicode font and works best with a <b><code>&nbsp;15091â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;3571ğŸ´</code></b> [solarized](https://github.com/altercation/solarized) terminal.
- <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;3â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;1ğŸ´</code></b> [agnoster-fseguin](https://github.com/fsegouin/oh-my-zsh-agnoster-mod-theme) - ğŸŒ [agnoster](https://gist.github.com/agnoster/3712874) variant with a right prompt.

Includes `git` status decorations.
- <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;1â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;0ğŸ´</code></b> [z4rr3t](https://github.com/inimicus/z4rr3t) - Based on sindresorhus' <b><code>&nbsp;11117â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;900ğŸ´</code></b> [pure](https://github.com/sindresorhus/pure) theme.
- <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;0â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;0ğŸ´</code></b> [zcraft](https://github.com/cpea2506/zcraft) - Minimalist theme with decorations for `git` status, last command exit status and the time taken by the last command.
- <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;2â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;2ğŸ´</code></b> [zelda](https://github.com/SuperKnerdBros/zelda.zsh-theme) Zelda-inspired theme. Includes `git` status decorations.
- <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;7â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;4ğŸ´</code></b> [zemm-blinks](https://github.com/aranasaurus/zemm-blinks.zsh-theme) - Customized version of oh-my-zsh <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;?â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;?ğŸ´</code></b> [blinks](https://github.com/ohmyzsh/ohmyzsh/blob/master/themes/blinks.zsh-theme) with mercurial support and other changes.
- <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;4â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;1ğŸ´</code></b> [zemoji](https://github.com/therzka/zemoji) - Based on ğŸŒ [wild-cherry]( https://github.com/mashaal/wild-cherry/tree/master/zsh). Includes exit status, `virtualenv`, `nvm`, `rvm` and `git` status decorations.
- <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;15â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;4ğŸ´</code></b> [zero](https://github.com/arlimus/zero.zsh) - Zero's theme & plugin. Has variants for both light and dark terminal backgrounds.
- <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;3â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;0ğŸ´</code></b> [zeroastro](https://github.com/zeroastro/zeroastro-zsh-theme) - Works best on dark backgrounds, includes `git` status decorations.
- <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;0â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;0ğŸ´</code></b> [zerocake](https://github.com/ZeroPoke/ZeroCake.zsh-theme) - Works better on dark brackgrounds.
- <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;0â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;0ğŸ´</code></b> [zest](https://github.com/hash-bang/zsh-theme-zest) - A functional theme for ZSH. Influenced by <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;78â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;28ğŸ´</code></b> [zsh2000](https://github.com/consolemaverick/zsh2000), ğŸŒ [agnoster](https://gist.github.com/agnoster/3712874) and <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;1089â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;245ğŸ´</code></b> [powerline](https://github.com/jeremyFreeAgent/oh-my-zsh-powerline-theme) themes.
- <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;200â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;66ğŸ´</code></b> [zeta](https://github.com/skylerlee/zeta-zsh-theme) - Shows username, `git` status information, machine name, the current working directory and success/fail status of last command.
- ğŸŒ [zinc](https://gitlab.com/robobenklein/zinc) - A blazing-fast, pure ZSH, mixed asynchronous powerline prompt that's easily extensible and extremely configurable.
- <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;1â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;0ğŸ´</code></b> [zlambda](https://github.com/wdhg/zlambda) - Minimalist, includes `git` decorations without special font requirements.
- <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;0â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;0ğŸ´</code></b> [zodiac](https://github.com/adamalsen/zsh-zodiac) - Includes an emoji for the animal corresponding to the current year.
- <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;0â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;0ğŸ´</code></b> [zprompts](https://github.com/z-shell/zprompts) - Themes (prompts) that use original `zsh` theming subsystem.
- <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;2â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;1ğŸ´</code></b> [zqt](https://github.com/ladychili/zqt-zsh-theme) - Modified version of oh-my-zsh's <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;?â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;?ğŸ´</code></b> [maran](https://github.com/ohmyzsh/ohmyzsh/blob/master/themes/maran.zsh-theme) theme.
- <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;3â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;0ğŸ´</code></b> [zsh1999](https://github.com/DTan13/zsh1999) - Includes network connectivity, battery and `git` status decorations.
- <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;78â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;28ğŸ´</code></b> [zsh2000](https://github.com/consolemaverick/zsh2000) - Powerline looking ZSH theme which includes the `rvm` prompt, `git` status and branch, current time, user, hostname, pwd, exit status, whether running as root and background job status.
- <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;0â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;0ğŸ´</code></b> [zsh313](https://github.com/amirali313/zsh313-theme) - Minimal theme with `git` status decorations.
- <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;7â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;0ğŸ´</code></b> [zshcomrade](https://github.com/landongn/zshcomrade) - A ZSH theme, comrade!
- <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;8â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;2ğŸ´</code></b> [zshpower](https://github.com/snakypy/zshpower) - Optimized for python developers. Includes `git` and `pyenv` status decorations, username and host. Tries to install other plugins and fonts, so read its instructions before installing.
- <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;1â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;0ğŸ´</code></b> [zshred](https://github.com/redxtech/zshred) - Shows current directory, `git` decorations, exit status of last command and time.
- <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;0â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;0ğŸ´</code></b> [zwsh](https://github.com/naens/zwsh) - A Zpm3/Wordstar mode/theme for ZSH.
- <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;9â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;3ğŸ´</code></b> [zys](https://github.com/ZYSzys/zys-zsh-theme) - Similar to <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;3381â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;551ğŸ´</code></b> [Agnoster](https://github.com/agnoster/agnoster-zsh-theme), designed to disclose information contextually, with a powerline aesthetic.
- <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;0â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;0ğŸ´</code></b> [zzshell](https://github.com/thezzisu/zzshell) - Inspired by the default ğŸŒ [Oh-My-Zsh](http://ohmyz.sh/) theme. Displays exit code and `git` status decorations. Doesn't require Powerline fonts.

## Fonts

Some of the themes listed here require Powerline-compatible fonts, here are a few:

- <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;2286â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;228ğŸ´</code></b> [Awesome Terminal Fonts](https://github.com/gabrielelana/awesome-terminal-fonts) - A family of fonts that includes some nice monospaced Icons.
- <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;31â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;4ğŸ´</code></b> [Fantasque Awesome Font](https://github.com/ztomer/fantasque_awesome_powerline) - A nice monospaced font, patched with Font-Awesome, Octoicons and Powerline-Glyphs.
- <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;5888â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;143ğŸ´</code></b> [Fantasque-sans](https://github.com/belluzj/fantasque-sans) - Another Powerline-compatible font.
- ğŸŒ [Hack](https://sourcefoundry.org/hack/) - Another Powerline-compatible font designed specifically for source code.
- ğŸŒ [Input Mono](https://store.typenetwork.com/foundry/djr/series/input?family=input-mono) - A family of fonts designed specifically for code. It offers both monospaced and proportional fonts and includes powerline glyphs.
- <b><code>&nbsp;13606â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;444ğŸ´</code></b> [Iosevka](https://github.com/be5invis/Iosevka) - Codersâ€™ typeface, built from code. Highly customizable.
- ğŸŒ [Monoid](https://larsenwork.com/monoid/) - Monoid is customizable and optimized for coding with bitmap-like sharpness at 15px line-height even on low res displays.
- <b><code>&nbsp;33804â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;2635ğŸ´</code></b> [Nerd Fonts](https://github.com/ryanoasis/nerd-fonts) - Collection of over 20 patched fonts (over 2,000 variations) & FontForge font patcher python script for Powerline, Font Awesome, Octicons, Devicons, and Vim Devicons. Includes: Droid Sans, Meslo, Source Code, AnonymousPro, Hack, ProFont, Inconsolata, and many more.
- <b><code>&nbsp;23004â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;3111ğŸ´</code></b> [Powerline patched font collection](https://github.com/powerline/fonts) - A collection of a dozen or so fonts patched to include powerline gylphs.
- ğŸŒ [Terminus](http://files.ax86.net/terminus-ttf/) - TTF version of Terminus that includes powerline glyphs.

## Installation

### <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;6952â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;273ğŸ´</code></b> [Antigen](https://github.com/zsh-users/antigen)

Most of these plugins can be installed by adding `antigen bundle githubuser/reponame` to your .zshrc file. Antigen will handle cloning the plugin for you automatically the next time you start `zsh`. You can also add the plugin to a running ZSH with `antigen bundle githubuser/reponame` for testing before adding it to your `.zshrc`.

### <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;201â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;36ğŸ´</code></b> [dotzsh](https://github.com/dotphiles/dotzsh)

1. Clone new plugins into `.zsh.local/modules`
2. Load the plugin module in `.zshrc`
3. Open a new ZSH terminal window or tab

### ğŸŒ [Oh-My-Zsh](http://ohmyz.sh/)

1. `cd ~/.oh-my-zsh/custom/plugins`
2. `git clone repo`
3. Add the repo to your plugin list

### <b><code>&nbsp;12635â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;4440ğŸ´</code></b> [Prezto](https://github.com/sorin-ionescu/prezto)

1. Clone the plugin into your prezto modules directory
2. Add the plugin to your `.zpreztorc` file
3. Open a new terminal window or tab

### <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;1360â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;103ğŸ´</code></b> [Zgen](https://github.com/tarjoilija/zgen)

Zgen is not being actively maintained. Consider switching to the <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;168â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;8ğŸ´</code></b> [Zgenom](https://github.com/jandamm/zgenom) fork, which is.

### <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;168â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;8ğŸ´</code></b> [Zgenom](https://github.com/jandamm/zgenom)

Most of these plugins can be installed by adding `zgenom load githubuser/reponame` to your .zshrc file in the same function you're doing your other `zgenom load` calls in.

Zgenom will automatically clone the plugin repositories for you when you do a `zgenom save`.

### <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;4938â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;215ğŸ´</code></b> [zplug](https://github.com/zplug/zplug)

Most of these plugins can be installed by adding `zplug "githubuser/reponame"` to your `.zshrc` file.

### <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;218â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;11ğŸ´</code></b> [zpm](https://github.com/zpm-zsh/zpm)

Most of these plugins can be installed by adding `zpm load "githubuser/reponame"` to your `.zshrc` file.

## Writing New Plugins and Themes

I've documented some recommendations for writing new plugin and themes <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;?â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;?ğŸ´</code></b> [here](https://github.com/unixorn/awesome-zsh-plugins/blob/master/Writing_Plugins_and_Themes.md).

There is also a more detailed ğŸŒ [Zsh Plugin Standard](https://zdharma-continuum.github.io/Zsh-100-Commits-Club/Zsh-Plugin-Standard.html).

## Other Resources

### ZSH Tools

- <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;615â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;50ğŸ´</code></b> [ShellSpec](https://github.com/shellspec/shellspec) - A full-featured BDD unit testing framework for dash, bash, ksh, ZSH and all POSIX shells.
- <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;154â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;9ğŸ´</code></b> [zsh-bench](https://github.com/romkatv/zsh-bench) - A benchmark for interactive ZSH. It measures user-visible latency of interactive `zsh`: input lag, command lag, etc
- <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;231â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;17ğŸ´</code></b> [zshdb](https://github.com/rocky/zshdb) - A ZSH debugger.
- <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;2â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;1ğŸ´</code></b> [zshelldoc](https://github.com/zdharma-continuum/zshelldoc) - Doxygen for shell scripts. Parses ZSH and Bash scripts, outputs Asciidoc document with function lists, call trees, lists of exported variables, and more.
- <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;159â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;18ğŸ´</code></b> [zunit](https://github.com/zunit-zsh/zunit) - A powerful unit testing framework for ZSH.

### Other References

- The ğŸŒ [ZSH Reference Card](http://www.bash2zsh.com/zsh_refcard/refcard.pdf) and ğŸŒ [zsh-lovers site](https://grml.org/zsh/zsh-lovers.html) are indispensable.

- <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;722â­</code></b> <b><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;49ğŸ´</code></b> [Mastering ZSH](https://github.com/rothgar/mastering-zsh) is a great tutorial that builds on the basics to show you advanced ZSH usage, customizations, and practical examples.
